						<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
					</div>
					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Highly_composite_numbers.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Highly_composite_numbers.svg/250px-Highly_composite_numbers.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="333" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Highly_composite_numbers.svg/375px-Highly_composite_numbers.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Highly_composite_numbers.svg/500px-Highly_composite_numbers.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="683" /></a><figcaption>Plot of the number of divisors of integers from 1 to 1000. Highly composite numbers are in bold and superior highly composite numbers are starred. In the <a class="external text" href="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/Highly_composite_numbers.svg">SVG</a> file, hover over a bar to see its statistics.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The tables below list all of the <a href="/wiki/Divisors" class="mw-redirect" title="Divisors">divisors</a> of the numbers 1 to 1000.
</p><p>A divisor of an <a href="/wiki/Integer" title="Integer">integer</a> <i>n</i> is an integer <i>m</i>, for which <i>n</i>/<i>m</i> is again an integer (which is necessarily also a divisor of <i>n</i>). For example, 3 is a divisor of 21, since 21/7&#160;=&#160;3 (and therefore 7 is also a divisor of 21).
</p><p>If <i>m</i> is a divisor of <i>n</i>, then so is &#8722;<i>m</i>. The tables below only list positive divisors.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Key_to_the_tables">Key to the tables</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Table_of_divisors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Key to the tables"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Divisor_function" title="Divisor function"> <i>d</i>(<i>n</i>)</a> is the number of positive divisors of <i>n</i>, including 1 and <i>n</i> itself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Divisor_function" title="Divisor function"> σ(<i>n</i>)</a> is the sum of the positive divisors of <i>n</i>, including 1 and <i>n</i> itself</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Divisor_function" title="Divisor function"> <i>s</i>(<i>n</i>)</a> is the sum of the proper divisors of <i>n</i>, including 1 but not <i>n</i> itself; that is,  <i>s</i>(<i>n</i>)&#160;=&#160;σ(<i>n</i>)&#160;&#8722;&#160;<i>n</i></li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Deficient_number" title="Deficient number">deficient number</a> is greater than the sum of its proper divisors; that is, <i>s</i>(<i>n</i>)&#160;&lt;&#160;<i>n</i></li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Perfect_number" title="Perfect number">perfect number</a> equals the sum of its proper divisors; that is, <i>s</i>(<i>n</i>)&#160;=&#160;<i>n</i></li>
<li>an <a href="/wiki/Abundant_number" title="Abundant number">abundant number</a> is lesser than the sum of its proper divisors; that is, <i>s</i>(<i>n</i>)&#160;&gt;&#160;<i>n</i></li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Highly_abundant_number" title="Highly abundant number">highly abundant number</a> has a sum of positive divisors that is greater than any lesser number; that is, σ(<i>n</i>) &gt; σ(<i>m</i>) <i>for every positive integer m</i> &lt; <i>n</i>. Counterintuitively, the first seven <i>highly abundant</i> numbers are not <i>abundant</i> numbers.</li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Prime_number" title="Prime number">prime number</a> has only 1 and itself as divisors; that is, <i>d</i>(<i>n</i>)&#160;=&#160;2</li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Composite_number" title="Composite number">composite number</a> has more than just 1 and itself as divisors; that is, <i>d</i>(<i>n</i>)&#160;&gt;&#160;2</li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Highly_composite_number" title="Highly composite number">highly composite number</a> has a number of positive divisors that is greater than any lesser number; that is, <i>d</i>(<i>n</i>) &gt; <i>d</i>(<i>m</i>) <i>for every positive integer m</i> &lt; <i>n</i>. Counterintuitively, the first two <i>highly composite</i> numbers are not <i>composite</i> numbers.</li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Superior_highly_composite_number" title="Superior highly composite number">superior highly composite number</a> has a ratio between its number of divisors and itself raised to some positive power that equals or is greater than any other number; that is, <i>there exists some ε such that</i> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {d(n)}{n^{\varepsilon }}}\geq {\frac {d(m)}{m^{\varepsilon }}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>d</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mi>n</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
            </mrow>
            <msup>
              <mi>n</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>&#x03B5;<!-- ε --></mi>
              </mrow>
            </msup>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>&#x2265;<!-- ≥ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>d</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mi>m</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
            </mrow>
            <msup>
              <mi>m</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>&#x03B5;<!-- ε --></mi>
              </mrow>
            </msup>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {d(n)}{n^{\varepsilon }}}\geq {\frac {d(m)}{m^{\varepsilon }}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8c1a1652b63a35a3c7f3f807151cb4383f58beb9" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:14.256ex; height:5.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {d(n)}{n^{\varepsilon }}}\geq {\frac {d(m)}{m^{\varepsilon }}}}"></span> <i>for every other positive integer m</i></li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Primitive_abundant_number" title="Primitive abundant number">primitive abundant number</a> is an <i>abundant</i> number whose proper divisors are all <i>deficient</i> numbers</li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/Weird_number" title="Weird number">weird number</a> is an <i>abundant</i> number that is not <a href="/wiki/Semiperfect" class="mw-redirect" title="Semiperfect">semiperfect</a>; that is, <i>no subset of the proper divisors of n sum to n</i></li></ul>
